<p>The <b>2016–17 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team</b> represented <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_basketball_season" title="2016–17 NCAA Division I men's basketball season">2016–17 NCAA Division I men's basketball season</a>. The Hoyas, led by 13th-year head coach <a href="/wiki/John_Thompson_III" title="John Thompson III">John Thompson III</a>, played their home games at the <a href="/wiki/Capital_One_Arena" title="Capital One Arena">Verizon Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, and were members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">Big East Conference</a>.
</p><p>The season saw the return of <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Wallace" title="Jonathan Wallace">Jonathan Wallace</a>, the Hoyas′ standout <a href="/wiki/Point_guard" title="Point guard">point guard</a> from <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2004–05 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2004</a> to <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2007–08 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2008</a>, to the basketball program as a special assistant after eight seasons playing professional basketball in the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Summer_League" title="NBA Summer League">NBA Summer League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> Developmental League, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Hoyas finished the season at 14–18, 5–13 in <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Big_East_Conference_men%27s_basketball_season" title="2016–17 Big East Conference men's basketball season">Big East play</a>, to finish in ninth place in the conference. As the No. 9 seed in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Big_East_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2017 Big East Men's Basketball Tournament">Big East Tournament</a>, they lost in the first round to <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_St._John%27s_Red_Storm_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 St. John's Red Storm men's basketball team">St. John's</a>. Georgetown finished the season with a losing record for the second straight year, the first time that had happened since the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1971–72 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1972</a> and <a href="/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1972–73 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1973</a> seasons, and without an invitation to a postseason tournament in consecutive years since 1972 and 1973.
</p><p>On March 23, 2017, Georgetown officials announced that John Thompson III had been <a href="/wiki/Dismissal_(employment)" title="Dismissal (employment)">fired</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> On April 2, it was reported that <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">Basketball Hall of Famer</a> and Georgetown alum <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing" title="Patrick Ewing">Patrick Ewing</a> would replace Thompson as head coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Roster"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Roster</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Schedule"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Schedule</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Previous_season">Previous season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Previous season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">Hoyas</a> finished the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_basketball_season" title="2015–16 NCAA Division I men's basketball season">2015–16 season</a> 15–18, 7–11 in <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Big_East_Conference_men%27s_basketball_season" title="2015–16 Big East Conference men's basketball season">Big East play</a> to finish in eighth place. They defeated <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_DePaul_Blue_Demons_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 DePaul Blue Demons men's basketball team">DePaul</a> in the first round of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Big_East_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2016 Big East Men's Basketball Tournament">Big East Tournament</a> to advance to the quarterfinals where they lost to <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Villanova_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 Villanova Wildcats men's basketball team">Villanova</a>. For the first time in John Thompson III's twelve years as head coach, the Hoyas did not make a postseason tournament.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preseason">Preseason</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preseason">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Prior to the season, Georgetown was picked to finish in a tie for fourth place in a poll of Big East coaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-6">[6]</a></sup> Isaac Copeland was named to the preseason All-Big East second team and <a href="/wiki/L._J._Peak" title="L. J. Peak">L. J. Peak</a> received an Honorable Mention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_recap">Season recap</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Season recap">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Georgetown had lost three players since the conclusion of <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">the previous season</a>. Little-used <a href="/wiki/Walk-on_(sports)" title="Walk-on (sports)">walk-on</a> senior <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guard_(basketball)" title="Guard (basketball)">guard</a> Riyan Williams – the son of Georgetown great <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Williams_(basketball,_born_1964)" title="Reggie Williams (basketball, born 1964)">Reggie Williams</a> – had graduated with a year of college eligibility remaining and chose to transfer to <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_II" title="NCAA Division II">NCAA Division II</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goldey-Beacom_College" title="Goldey-Beacom College">Goldey-Beacom College</a> to play his final year of <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">college basketball</a>, and sophomore <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forward_(basketball)" title="Forward (basketball)">forward</a> Paul White, the team's leading scorer off the bench during <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2014–15 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">his freshman year</a> but limited by a hip injury to seven games during the 2015–2016 season, had transferred to <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Ducks_men%27s_basketball" title="Oregon Ducks men's basketball">Oregon</a> at the end of August 2016. By far the team's biggest loss, however, was guard <a href="/wiki/D%27Vauntes_Smith-Rivera" title="D'Vauntes Smith-Rivera">D'Vauntes Smith-Rivera</a>, whose graduation in 2016 left the Hoyas without their leading scorer of the past three seasons. Although a natural <a href="/wiki/Shooting_guard" title="Shooting guard">shooting guard</a> who finished his college career as Georgetown's fifth-leading all-time scorer<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamaria20160310_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-santamaria20160310-7">[7]</a></sup> and with more three-pointers made than any previous Hoya,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamaria20160310_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-santamaria20160310-7">[7]</a></sup> Smith-Rivera had also served as the team's <a href="/wiki/Point_guard" title="Point guard">point guard</a> for the past two seasons, and the team keenly felt the loss of both his scoring ability and his in-game leadership.
</p><p>At forward, senior Reggie Cameron, juniors Isaac Copeland, Trey Mourning, and <a href="/wiki/L._J._Peak" title="L. J. Peak">L. J. Peak</a>, and sophomores <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Derrickson" title="Marcus Derrickson">Marcus Derrickson</a> and Kaleb Johnson all returned for 2016–2017. Junior guard Tre Campbell and sophomore <a href="/wiki/Center_(basketball)" title="Center (basketball)">center</a> Jesse Govan also came back for another season. Forward Akoy Agau, who had transferred from <a href="/wiki/Louisville_Cardinals_men%27s_basketball" title="Louisville Cardinals men's basketball">Louisville</a> in January 2015 and had planned to begin play for Georgetown in January 2016 after sitting out the two full semesters the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> mandated for transferring players, had missed the entire 2015–2016 season while recovering from knee surgery,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> but he finally would make his Georgetown debut in 2016–2017 as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Redshirt_(sports)" title="Redshirt (sports)">redshirt</a> junior. A surprise returnee from the previous season was fifth-year senior center Bradley Hayes; he was due to graduate in 2016, and virtually everyone, including Hayes himself, believed as the 2015–2016 season came to an end that his college career was over. However, John Thompson III applied for an NCAA waiver that would allow Hayes to return for a fifth year as a redshirt senior in 2016–2017<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamaria20160429_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-santamaria20160429-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dauster20170118_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-dauster20170118-10">[10]</a></sup> because he had played in only nine games and for only 14 minutes during <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2012–13 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">his freshman year</a> and had a semester to go to complete his degree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dauster20170118_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-dauster20170118-10">[10]</a></sup> The NCAA granted the waiver, provided that Hayes sat out the first four games of the 2016–2017 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dauster20170118_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-dauster20170118-10">[10]</a></sup> The team's former student manager, junior guard Ra'Mond Hines, who had made the team for the first time as a walk-on late the previous season, also returned to the team for 2016–2017, again as a walk-on.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two freshmen joined the team, guard Jagan Moseley and walk-on forward George Muresan, the son of former <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> center <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gheorghe_Muresan" title="Gheorghe Muresan">Gheorghe Muresan</a>. Also arriving for the year were two upperclassmen. Guard Rodney Pryor had transferred from <a href="/wiki/Robert_Morris_Colonials_men%27s_basketball" title="Robert Morris Colonials men's basketball">Robert Morris</a> and was eligible to play for Georgetown immediately as a redshirt senior because he had graduated from Robert Morris the previous spring. Junior guard Jonathan Mulmore, a <a href="/wiki/Junior_college" title="Junior college">junior college</a> transfer from <a href="/wiki/Allegany_College_of_Maryland" title="Allegany College of Maryland">Allegany College of Maryland</a>, also joined the team.
</p><p>The 2016–2017 squad's athleticism raised the prospect of Georgetown playing a more uptempo game than had been the custom during the 12 previous seasons under John Thompson III, who favored the more deliberate "<a href="/wiki/Princeton_offense" title="Princeton offense">Princeton offense</a>";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> during the offseason, Thompson had revamped his coaching staff and discussed at length the idea of adopting his system to accommodate a new style of play,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> promising a faster team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> Although the shadow of the losing season the previous year hung over the returning players, the 2016–2017 season began with qualified optimism because of the number of experienced players on the roster and Georgetown's size relative to other teams in the Big East, which had lost a number of notable "big men" over the offseason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-novak20161111_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-novak20161111-16">[16]</a></sup> At least some observers considered Georgetown's frontcourt a strength<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-novak20161111_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-novak20161111-16">[16]</a></sup> and deemed it unlikely that Georgetown would suffer through another uncharacteristically mediocre season because of the Hoyas′ pattern of recurring success over many years and quick recoveries from the occasional poor seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-novak20161111_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-novak20161111-16">[16]</a></sup> But the Hoyas faced a particularly challenging early nonconference schedule,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-novak20161111_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-novak20161111-16">[16]</a></sup> and the departure of Smith-Rivera left questions as to how well the backcourt would perform and who would step up to lead the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-novak20161111_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-novak20161111-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nonconference_schedule">Nonconference schedule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Nonconference schedule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Georgetown began its season by defeating <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_USC_Upstate_Spartans_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 USC Upstate Spartans men's basketball team">South Carolina Upstate</a> in a game at the Verizon Center in which the Hoyas started only one player (Isaac Copeland) who had started their final game of the previous season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> Georgetown displayed a very different style of play from that seen previously under John Thompson III, with frequent presses and more running,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> and won 105–60.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> It was Georgetown's greatest offensive output since the Hoyas scored 111 points against <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Missouri_Tigers_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Missouri Tigers men's basketball team">Missouri</a> in an overtime victory on <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">November 30, 2010</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> the fifth time the Hoyas had scored 100 or more points in a game during John Thompson III's 13 seasons as head coach,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161112_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161112-17">[17]</a></sup> and the third-highest scoring output of Thompson's tenure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> It was the highest-scoring season opener under Thompson,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> the first 100-plus-point season opener for Georgetown since they beat <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III" title="NCAA Division III">NCAA Division III</a> <a href="/wiki/Marymount_University" title="Marymount University">Marymount</a> 108–47 to start the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2001–02 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2001–2002 season</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-7"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> and the first time the Hoyas had scored 100 points or more in a season opener against an <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> opponent since defeating <a href="/wiki/Colgate_Raiders_men%27s_basketball" title="Colgate Raiders men's basketball">Colgate</a> 106-57 to begin the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1995–96 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1995–1996 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-8"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> Making his Hoya debut, Rodney Pryor sank a career-high six three-pointers on eight attempts from beyond the arc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161112_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161112-17">[17]</a></sup> and shot 13-of-16 (81.3 percent) from the field overall<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161112_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161112-17">[17]</a></sup> on the way to a 32-point game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161112_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161112-17">[17]</a></sup> Pryor scored 26 points in the first half alone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161112_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161112-17">[17]</a></sup> and the 68 points the Hoyas scored by halftime set a school record for first-half points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161112_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161112-17">[17]</a></sup> eclipsing the 57 points they scored in the first half against <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Savannah_State_Tigers_basketball_team" title="2008–09 Savannah State Tigers basketball team">Savannah State</a> on <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2008–09 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">December 8, 2008</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-9"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> and it was the highest-scoring half for Georgetown in the 21st century to that point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-10"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> Overall, the Hoyas shot 66.7 percent from the field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevens20161112_15-11"><a href="#cite_note-stevens20161112-15">[15]</a></sup> and L. J. Peak scored 14 points against the Spartans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161112_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161112-17">[17]</a></sup> Jesse Govan had 11,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161112_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161112-18">[18]</a></sup> Isaac Copeland scored 10,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161112_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161112-18">[18]</a></sup> and Tre Campbell came off the bench to add 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161112_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161112-18">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>Three days later, Georgetown took part in the annual <a href="/wiki/Gavitt_Tipoff_Games" title="Gavitt Tipoff Games">Gavitt Tipoff Games</a>, a series of eight games per year between teams of the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">Big East Conference</a> and <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. For the second straight year, Georgetown drew <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Maryland Terrapins men's basketball team">Maryland</a> as its Big Ten opponent, hosting the Terrapins at the Verizon Center – the first time the Hoyas had hosted the Terrapins since <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1993–94 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1993</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161115_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161115-19">[19]</a></sup> The Hoyas made 37 of their 42 free throws<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161115_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161115-19">[19]</a></sup> but blew a 68–59 lead with 2:21 remaining as Maryland went on a 17–7 scoring run the rest of the way to win the game, 76–75, defeating Georgetown for the second season in a row.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161115_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161115-19">[19]</a></sup> Maryland's players stormed the court to celebrate the victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161115_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161115-19">[19]</a></sup> Scoring 21 points, L. J. Peak<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161115_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161115-20">[20]</a></sup> led a balanced Georgetown attack which also saw Rodney Pryor score 14 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161115_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161115-20">[20]</a></sup> Isaac Copeland finish with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double-double" title="Double-double">double-double</a> (13 points and 13 rebounds),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161115_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161115-20">[20]</a></sup> and Jesse Govan add 12 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161115_20-3"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161115-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>Next up for the Hoyas was the <a href="/wiki/Maui_Invitational_Tournament" title="Maui Invitational Tournament">Maui Invitational Tournament</a>. Georgetown began the tournament by hosting a non-bracketed opening-round game against <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Arkansas_State_Red_Wolves_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Arkansas State Red Wolves men's basketball team">Arkansas State</a> at <a href="/wiki/McDonough_Gymnasium" title="McDonough Gymnasium">McDonough Gymnasium</a>, the Hoyas′ first game on campus since the <a href="/wiki/2014_National_Invitation_Tournament" title="2014 National Invitation Tournament">2014 National Invitation Tournament</a>. The Hoyas shot only 3-for-18 (16.7 percent) from three-point range<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161117_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161117-21">[21]</a></sup> and, despite Jesse Govan's 20 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161117_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161117-21">[21]</a></sup> L. J. Peak's 18,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161117_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161117-21">[21]</a></sup> and Isaac Copeland's 11,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> the Red Wolves led by double figures for much of the game<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161117_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161117-21">[21]</a></sup> and held off a 22-7 late-game Georgetown rally to upset the Hoyas 78–72.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161117_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161117-21">[21]</a></sup> Thanks to the surprising loss, Georgetown opened its season with a 1–2 record for the second straight year.
</p><p>Four days later, the Hoyas were in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Lahaina_Civic_Center" title="Lahaina Civic Center">Lahaina Civic Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lahaina,_Hawaii" title="Lahaina, Hawaii">Lahaina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maui" title="Maui">Maui</a>, to open the bracketed championship round of the tournament with a quarterfinal match-up against their first ranked opponent of the year, No. 13 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Oregon_Ducks_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Oregon Ducks men's basketball team">Oregon</a>. The Ducks struggled against a strong Hoya defense and did not score a field goal for the first six minutes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> shooting 7-for-29 (24.1 percent) from the field in the first half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor, meanwhile, led Georgetown through Oregon's pressure defense during the half, and his buzzer-beating three-pointer gave the Hoyas a 38–21 halftime lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> In the second half, however, the Ducks′ pressure defense was far more effective, and it allowed them to force turnovers and make easy transition baskets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> While Georgetown missed its first 12 shots of the second half,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> Oregon opened the half with a 22–4 scoring run that gave the Ducks a 43–42 lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> The Hoyas then staged a 10–2 scoring run of their own to pull out to a 52–45 lead with three minutes to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> Oregon responded with a late run and, with 3.8 seconds remaining, closed to a 63–61 deficit on a long three-pointer by junior forward <a href="/wiki/Dillon_Brooks" title="Dillon Brooks">Dillon Brooks</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> but L. J. Peak hit two free throws with 2.7 seconds to play to secure a 65–61 upset Georgetown victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> Pryor had a double-double with 26 points and 10 rebounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> and Peak finished with 17 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup> The Hoyas evened their record at 2–2, but had begun to show a tendency toward inconsistent play during their first four games, sometimes playing dominating basketball and then struggling mightily during other stretches of their games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161121_23-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161121-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Hoyas advanced to the semifinals the next day to meet another ranked opponent, No. 16 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Wisconsin_Badgers_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Wisconsin Badgers men's basketball team">Wisconsin</a>, which had defeated <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Tennessee_Volunteers_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Tennessee Volunteers basketball team">Tennessee</a> in the quarterfinals the previous day. The Hoyas never really found their shooting touch, but they held their own in the first half and Wisconsin clung to a 32–29 lead at halftime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> During the second half, however, the Badgers opened with a scoring run that gave them a 44–34 lead,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> and by midway through the half led 53–39<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> on their way to a 73–57 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> During the game, Wisconsin shot only 5-for-22 (22.7 percent) from three-point range,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> but rebounding proved to be the game's decisive factor: Wisconsin had a 19-1 advantage in offensive rebounds<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> and scored 20 second-chance points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> and overall the Badgers outrebounded the Hoyas 50-21<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> and outscored Georgetown 38–16 in the paint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> The Hoyas′ poor performance on the boards prompted John Thompson III to observe during his post-game comments, "We have to get some guys that understand that it′s not just about points and minutes, and care about all aspects of the game."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> L. J. Peak led the Hoyas with 18 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> and Rodney Pryor finished with 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161122_24-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161122-24">[24]</a></sup> For the second straight season, the Hoyas opened with a 2–3 record.
</p><p>The loss to Wisconsin relegated the Hoyas to the third-place game, in which they faced <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Oklahoma_State_Cowboys_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Oklahoma State Cowboys basketball team">Oklahoma State</a> the next day. Oklahoma State had beaten <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UConn_Huskies_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 UConn Huskies men's basketball team">UConn</a> in the quarterfinals, but then suffered a one-sided defeat at the hands of No. 4 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball team">North Carolina</a> in the semifinals. The Cowboys began the game with a sluggish and lackluster effort that led Oklahoma State head coach <a href="/wiki/Brad_Underwood" title="Brad Underwood">Brad Underwood</a> to call an early time out, slam down his clipboard, berate his team, and replace four starters with bench players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> Underwood's admonishment and the lineup change sparked much greater energy among his players, who presented the Hoyas with a strong pressure defense the rest of the way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> This time, turnovers were the decisive factor: The Hoyas fell victim to sloppy ball-handling, and Oklahoma State forced 14 turnovers – 11 of them steals – in the first half alone<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> and led 50–35 at the half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> For the game overall, Georgetown shot 51 percent from the field, but Oklahoma State scored 41 points off 28 turnovers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> including 19 steals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> and had a 59–16 advantage in points off the bench.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor scored 15 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> and Bradley Hayes 13,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> and Akoy Agau scored in double figures for the first time as a Hoya, finishing with 11 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> but the Cowboys won 97–70.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161123_25-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161123-25">[25]</a></sup> Georgetown finished in fourth place in the tournament and fell to 2–4 on the season. It was Georgetown's worst start since the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1971–72 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1971–1972 team</a> opened 1–5 on its way to a 3–23 final record.
</p><p>The Hoyas returned to the Verizon Center to sweep a three-game homestand, defeating <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Howard_Bison_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Howard Bison basketball team">Howard</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Coppin_State_Eagles_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Coppin State Eagles men's basketball team">Coppin State</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Elon_Phoenix_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Elon Phoenix men's basketball team">Elon</a>; the Elon game, by far the closest of the three, was a part of the annual <a href="/wiki/BB%26T_Classic" title="BB&amp;T Classic">BB&amp;T Classic</a>, in which Georgetown made both its third consecutive appearance and third appearance overall and improved its all-time record in the Classic to 3–0. Rodney Pryor led the Hoyas in all three games; he scored 26 points against Howard<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161127_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161127-27">[27]</a></sup> and 30 points against Coppin State, tying his career high with seven three-pointers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161130_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161130-28">[28]</a></sup> and he finished with 23 points against Elon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161204_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161204-29">[29]</a></sup> L. J. Peak scored 14 points against Howard<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161127_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161127-27">[27]</a></sup> and had a career-high 10 assists<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161130_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161130-28">[28]</a></sup> against Coppin State – the first Georgetown player to have double-digit assists since <a href="/wiki/Markel_Starks" title="Markel Starks">Markel Starks</a> had 11 on <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2013–14 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">March 3, 2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161130_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161130-28">[28]</a></sup> Peak followed that performance with a 22-point game against Elon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161204_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161204-29">[29]</a></sup> Akoy Agau scored 14 against Howard,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161127_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161127-27">[27]</a></sup> a new high for him as a Hoya, and Tre Campbell finished with 12 points in the Howard game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161127_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161127-27">[27]</a></sup> Bradley Hayes had 10 points, seven rebounds, five assists, and three blocked shots against Coppin State,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161130_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161130-28">[28]</a></sup> while Jessie Govan grabbed a career-best 11 rebounds in the Coppin State game<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161130_28-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161130-28">[28]</a></sup> and scored 13 points against Elon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161204_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161204-29">[29]</a></sup> Against Coppin State, the Hoyas shot 45.2 percent from three-point range, making a season-high 14 three-pointers on 31 attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161130_28-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161130-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p><p>Six days after beating Elon, Georgetown traveled to <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> to meet <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_La_Salle_Explorers_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 La Salle Explorers men's basketball team">La Salle</a> – a team Georgetown had met only twice since <a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1964–65 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1965</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161210_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161210-30">[30]</a></sup> – in the Hoophall Miami Invitational.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161210_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161210-30">[30]</a></sup> The Hoyas broke a tie and ran away from the Explorers with a late run in the final 8:44 to win,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161210_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161210-30">[30]</a></sup> improving their all-time record against La Salle to 10–15<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161210_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161210-30">[30]</a></sup> and extending their winning streak to four, as L. J. Peak scored 24 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161210_30-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161210-30">[30]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor 19,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161210_30-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161210-30">[30]</a></sup> Jesse Govan 18,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161210_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161210-31">[31]</a></sup> and Jagan Moseley scored in double figures for the first time as a Hoya with 14 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161210_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161210-31">[31]</a></sup> while Marcus Derrickson contributed nine points and eight rebounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161210_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161210-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 12, two days after the La Salle game, John Thompson III announced that Isaac Copeland had decided to transfer to <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Cornhuskers_men%27s_basketball" title="Nebraska Cornhuskers men's basketball">Nebraska</a> at the end of the semester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wang20161212_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-wang20161212-32">[32]</a></sup> Copeland gave no reason for leaving Georgetown, but the arrival of Rodney Pryor and increased playing time for reserves Marcus Derrickson and Kaleb Johnson as well as his own declining performance and injuries had led to reduced playing time for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wang20161212_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-wang20161212-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>After another week off following the La Salle game, the Hoyas journeyed to the <a href="/wiki/Carrier_Dome" title="Carrier Dome">Carrier Dome</a> to face <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Syracuse_Orange_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Syracuse Orange men's basketball team">Syracuse</a> – their archrival throughout the 34-season history of the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">original Big East Conference</a> of 1979–2013 – on a snowy day on which Syracuse honored former Orange great <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Washington_(basketball)" title="Dwayne Washington (basketball)">Dwayne "Pearl" Washington</a>, who had died of cancer in April 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> Syracuse jumped out to an 11–4 lead, its largest of the game, in the first 5:08,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> but Georgetown came back and L. J. Peak sank a basket to tie the game at 31–31 with two minutes left until the intermission,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> in part thanks to Peak's 12 first-half points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> The game was tied 33–33 at halftime,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-4"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> but Georgetown pulled ahead to its largest lead of the game, 67–60, with only 2:36 left to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-5"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> The Orange closed to 69–66 with 1:04 left,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-6"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> but the Hoyas hit nine free throws in the final 38 seconds to come away with a 78–71 victory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-7"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> their sixth over the Orange in the last eight meetings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-8"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> Peak had a double-double with 23 points and 11 rebounds<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-9"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> and Rodney Pryor scored 20 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-10"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> Georgetown, which entered the game averaging 28.5 trips to the free-throw line per game and shooting 77.5 percent in free throws,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-11"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> went 22-of-25 from the free-throw line, while Syracuse made only 14 of its 25 free throw attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-12"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> The Hoyas improved their all-time record against Syracuse to 43–49,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-13"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> their all-time road record against Syracuse to 13–30,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-14"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup> and their record against the Orange under John Thompson III to 11–7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kekis20161217_33-15"><a href="#cite_note-kekis20161217-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Georgetown closed out the nonconference portion of its season by returning to the Verizon Center to defeat <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UNC_Greensboro_Spartans_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 UNC Greensboro Spartans men's basketball team">UNC Greensboro</a> in a game in which Jesse Govan went 9-for-13 (69.2 percent) from the field, including 2-for-2 in three-pointers, and had 20 points, nine rebounds, five assists, and four blocks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161222_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161222-34">[34]</a></sup> while L. J. Peak contributed 16 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Marcus Derrickson scored 15 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161222_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161222-34">[34]</a></sup> and Rodney Pryor added 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20161222_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20161222-34">[34]</a></sup> The Hoyas had won five straight to enter the Big East season with a record of 8–4.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conference_schedule">Conference schedule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Conference schedule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Hoyas opened the Big East season with a loss at <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Marquette_Golden_Eagles_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Marquette Golden Eagles men's basketball team">Marquette</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> in which Rodney Pryor finished with 23 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161228_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161228-37">[37]</a></sup> Jesse Govan scored 11,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161228_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161228-37">[37]</a></sup> and Marcus Derrickson came off the bench for 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20161228_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20161228-37">[37]</a></sup> They then came home to host their third ranked opponent of the year, No. 17 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Xavier_Musketeers_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Xavier Musketeers men's basketball team">Xavier</a>, at the Verizon Center on <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> 2016. Xavier was one of four Big East teams ranked in the Top 17 at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Peak scored 16 points in the first half, and the underdog Hoyas led 38–36 at halftime<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> and pulled out to a six-point lead early in the second half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Xavier came back to tie the game at 54–54, but Peak completed a three-point play – scoring his last points of the game – to put Georgetown ahead 57–54 with 11:41 left to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Xavier increasingly used a 1-3-1 <a href="/wiki/Zone_defense" title="Zone defense">zone defense</a> as the second half progressed, and this gave the Musketeers greater defensive success against the Hoyas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Xavier took the lead for good at 62–59 with 8:23 remaining during a 13-5 scoring run that gave the Musketeers their largest lead of the game, 74–62, with 3:58 left to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor led a Georgetown comeback by scoring 10 points in a row, but his potential game-tying three-pointer missed with Xavier leading 77–74 and 24 seconds remaining. Although Georgetown held Xavier to 39 percent shooting from the field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> and rendered Xavier's leading scorer, junior guard <a href="/wiki/Trevon_Bluiett" title="Trevon Bluiett">Trevon Bluiett</a>, ineffective throughout the game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Musketeer redshirt sophomore guard <a href="/wiki/Edmond_Sumner" title="Edmond Sumner">Edmond Sumner</a>, playing on his birthday, scored a career-high 28 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> From the free-throw line, Xavier went 29-for-38 (76.3 percent)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> with Sumner alone going 14-for-17 (82.4 percent),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> while Georgetown as a team shot 14-for-23 (60.9 percent) from the line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Georgetown shot 50 percent from the field, and Peak finished with a team-high 21 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-12"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Pryor with 20,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-13"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> and Derrickson with 12,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> but Xavier held on to win, 81–76.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-14"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> Georgetown had its first 0–2 start in Big East play since <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2012–13 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">the 2012–2013 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-15"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>A visit to <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Providence_Friars_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Providence Friars men's basketball team">Providence</a> four days later to play the first game of 2017 resulted in a third loss<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170104_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170104-40">[40]</a></sup> and Georgetown's first 0-3 start in conference play since <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1999–2000 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">the 1999-2000 season</a>. Marcus Derrickson had a career-high 26 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170104_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170104-40">[40]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor scored 16,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and Akoy Agau had his first career double-double with 12 points and a career-best 12 rebounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170104_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170104-40">[40]</a></sup> but Georgetown remained winless on the road against the Friars since <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2011–12 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">February 18, 2012</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170101_38-16"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170101-38">[38]</a></sup> The Hoyas then hosted their second ranked conference opponent of the season, No. 18 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Butler_Bulldogs_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Butler Bulldogs men's basketball team">Butler</a>, which three days earlier had upset No. 1 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Villanova_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Villanova Wildcats men's basketball team">Villanova</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> Georgetown led 32–31 at halftime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> With a minute left to play, the Hoyas held a 66–63 lead,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbyplay20170107_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-playbyplay20170107-43">[43]</a></sup> but Butler sophomore center Nate Fowler's three-pointer tied the game at 66–66 with 58 seconds to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbyplay20170107_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-playbyplay20170107-43">[43]</a></sup> Jagan Moseley hit two free throws with 38 seconds on the clock to give the Hoyas a 68–66 lead,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbyplay20170107_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-playbyplay20170107-43">[43]</a></sup> but Fowler's two free throws with eight seconds left again tied the game at 68–68.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbyplay20170107_43-3"><a href="#cite_note-playbyplay20170107-43">[43]</a></sup> Georgetown had a chance to avoid overtime and pull off an upset, but L. J. Peak's attempt at a buzzer-beating turnaround jumper as time expired in regulation bounced off the rim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> Butler never trailed in overtime and took the lead for good with 3:04 to play on two free throws by redshirt senior guard <a href="/wiki/Kethan_Savage" title="Kethan Savage">Kethan Savage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> The Bulldogs won, 85–76, their third consecutive victory over the Hoyas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> The Hoyas outscored the Bulldogs 40–20 in the paint<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> and Butler shot only 39.1 percent from the field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> but the Bulldogs stayed in the game on 10-of-20 shooting from three-point range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> Peak scored a team-high 21 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> Jagan Moseley contributed a career-best 20,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-12"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> Marcus Derrickson contributed 14 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20170107_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20170107-44">[44]</a></sup> and Bradley Hayes narrowly missed a double-double with 10 points and nine rebounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20170107_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20170107-44">[44]</a></sup> but Rodney Pryor, the Big East's scoring co-leader entering the game, averaging 19.8 points, went scoreless on 0-for-8 shooting against a spirited defensive effort by Butler freshman guard <a href="/wiki/Kamar_Baldwin" title="Kamar Baldwin">Kamar Baldwin</a>, who also scored a career-high 16 points for the Bulldogs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-13"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> Georgetown saw its record fall to 8–8 and opened its conference season 0–4 for the first time since <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1998–99 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">the 1998-1999 season</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-14"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup> and, along with <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_DePaul_Blue_Demons_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 DePaul Blue Demons men's basketball team">DePaul</a>, was one of two teams still winless in the Big East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170107_42-15"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170107-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two days after the loss to Butler, Georgetown's four-game homestand continued with its first conference win, a runaway victory over <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_St._John%27s_Red_Storm_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 St. John's Red Storm men's basketball team">St. John's</a> – the Hoyas′ twelfth straight home win over the Red Storm – with L. J. Peak scoring 16 points that included a 10-for-10 free-throw shooting performance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170109_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170109-45">[45]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor and Jagan Moseley each scoring 13 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170109_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170109-45">[45]</a></sup> and Marcus Derrickson adding 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170109_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170109-45">[45]</a></sup> A break from conference action followed, as <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UConn_Huskies_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 UConn Huskies men's basketball team">UConn</a> visited the Verizon Center to conclude a home-and-home series begun <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">the previous season</a>. The Hoyas and Huskies were charter members of the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">original Big East Conference</a> in <a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1979–80 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1979</a> and had met each season throughout that conference's 34-year history, but the rivalry had lapsed when Georgetown left the conference in the summer of 2013 to join the new <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">Big East Conference</a> while UConn remained behind in the old conference, renamed the <a href="/wiki/American_Athletic_Conference" title="American Athletic Conference">American Athletic Conference</a> and marketed as "the American;" the two-season home-and-home series revived play between the teams after a two-season absence. UConn had won the previous year, but this time the Hoyas overcame a 14-point second-half deficit to beat the Huskies and improve their all-time record against UConn to 36–30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170114_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170114-46">[46]</a></sup> L. J. Peak scored 21 points, 16 of them in the second half,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170114_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170114-46">[46]</a></sup> Jesse Govan came off the bench to finish with 15,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170114_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170114-46">[46]</a></sup> and Rodney Pryor had 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170114_46-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170114-46">[46]</a></sup> Georgetown's two-game winning streak and four-game homestand both came to an end two days later, when Providence visited Georgetown and won easily to sweep the regular-season series between the teams and stretch its winning streak against the Hoyas to six.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170116_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170116-47">[47]</a></sup> Peak scored 13 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170116_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170116-47">[47]</a></sup> and Pryor 12,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170116_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170116-47">[47]</a></sup> but the Hoyas as a team shot only 18-for-55 (32.7 percent) from the field and only 5-for-23 (21.7 percent) from three-point range against the Friars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170116_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170116-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>With a conference record of 1–5 and an overall record of 10–9, Georgetown began a stretch of three straight games in seven days against ranked conference opponents. First they visited No. 22 Xavier. The Musketeers entered the game having lost three games in a row, all against ranked Big East teams, their longest losing streak in three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> Xavier clung to a 34–33 lead at halftime, but pulled out to a 12-point advantage in the second half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> The Hoyas came back to tie the game at 58–58, but Xavier then went on a decisive 12–3 scoring run to  take a 70–61 lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor scored 23 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> and L. J. Peak finished with 12, but fouling and rebounding undid the Hoyas;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> the Musketeers repeatedly drew fouls by driving the basket and went 36-for-49 from the free-throw line, while the Hoyas made 11 out of 14 free throws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> Xavier won 86–75,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> handing Georgetown its sixth loss in seven games<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> and dropping the Hoyas to 10–10 on the season and 1–6 in the Big East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170122_48-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170122-48">[48]</a></sup> In play against ranked teams, Georgetown had lost four straight games and nine of its last ten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>Georgetown next returned to the Verizon Center to host No. 16 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Creighton_Bluejays_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Creighton Bluejays men's basketball team">Creighton</a>. The Bluejays were the second-best shooting team in <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> at 52.8 percent from the field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> and tenth in three-point shooting at 40.8 percent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> but had suffered a major loss when a season-ending knee injury sidelined their <a href="/wiki/Point_guard" title="Point guard">point guard</a>, senior Maurice Watson Jr., nine days earlier during a game against Xavier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Jonathan Mulmore made his first start as a Hoya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor had an outstanding first half in which he dunked several times, sank two of his three three-pointers, and scored 15 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Thanks in part to a 13–2 scoring run,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Georgetown led 39–27 at the half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> The Hoyas extended their lead to as many as 22 points in the second half<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> and never led by fewer than 14 points during the last 15:32 of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Georgetown cruised to a 71–51 upset victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Creighton shot only 34.5 percent from the field and only 1-for-18 (5.6 percent) from three-point range,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> and it was the Bluejays′ lowest-scoring game of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-12"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Georgetown outrebounded Creighton 47–36.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-13"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> L. J. Peak scored 20 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-14"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> Pryor finished with 18,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20170125_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20170125-50">[50]</a></sup> and Jesse Govan added 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20170125_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20170125-50">[50]</a></sup> The win was Georgetown's first conference victory over any team other than <a href="/wiki/DePaul_Blue_Demons_men%27s_basketball" title="DePaul Blue Demons men's basketball">DePaul</a> and St. John's – perennially the two teams at the bottom of the conference's standings – since a win over <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Creighton_Bluejays_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 Creighton Bluejays men's basketball team">Creighton</a> on <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">January 26, 2016</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-15"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup> and it improved Georgetown's conference record to 2–6, allowing the Hoyas to avoid their first 1–7 conference start since the 1998-1999 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170125_49-16"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170125-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Hoyas traveled to <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis" title="Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a> to face No. 11 Butler in their next game. Butler – winner of four straight games overall and 14 straight at home, including 11–0 thus far in the 2016–2017 season<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> – led 41–40 at halftime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> During one stretch in the second half, Rodney Pryor, despite playing with four fouls, scored 11 straight points, nine of them on three straight contested three-pointers, giving Georgetown a 72–65 lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> The Bulldogs then closed the gap, scoring seven straight points to tie the game at 72–72.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> The Hoyas led 79–77 with 1:03 to play when Jesse Govan hit a long, unexpected three-pointer – only the third three-pointer he had ever made in Big East play – to give Georgetown an 82–77 lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> The Bulldogs never had another chance to tie or take the lead, and Georgetown won 85–81.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> During the three-year tenure of Butler head coach <a href="/wiki/Chris_Holtmann" title="Chris Holtmann">Chris Holtmann</a>, the Bulldogs had won all 30 previous games in which they had scored 80 or more points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> The Hoyas shot 63.8 percent from the field for the game and 72.7 percent in the second half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> L. J. Peak scored 22 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> and Pryor 20,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> while Govan went 8-for-9 from the field overall and 3-for-3 in three-pointers and tied his season high by finishing with 20 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>The back-to-back wins over Creighton and Butler gave the Hoyas a 3–3 record against ranked teams for the season<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> and, with a weaker part of their schedule coming up, raised hopes that the team could turn its season around after a difficult start over the first three months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170128_51-12"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170128-51">[51]</a></sup> The Hoyas concluded January by winning their third game in a row, defeating <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_DePaul_Blue_Demons_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 DePaul Blue Demons men's basketball team">DePaul</a> in a close one at the Verizon Center thanks largely to L. J. Peak scoring five points n the final minute and Jesse Govan blocking a shot with 40 seconds to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170131_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170131-52">[52]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor scored a game-high 26 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170131_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170131-52">[52]</a></sup> Govan finished with 14,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170131_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170131-52">[52]</a></sup> and Peak contributed 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170131_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170131-52">[52]</a></sup> The victory was Georgetown's 20th over DePaul in the last 21 meetings between the teams and improved Georgetown's record to 13–10 overall, 4–6 in the Big East, but the Hoyas were destined to win only one more game all season.
</p><p>The team's February collapse began with an overtime loss to <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Seton_Hall_Pirates_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Seton Hall Pirates men's basketball team">Seton Hall</a> at the Verizon Center on February 4 in which L. J. Peak scored 18 points, Rodney Pryor had 13, and Marcus Derrickson finished with nine points and eight rebounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> On February 6, as the Hoyas headed north through <a href="/wiki/Howard_County,_Maryland" title="Howard County, Maryland">Howard County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">Interstate 95</a> on their way to <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> to play No. 2 <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Villanova_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2016–17 Villanova Wildcats men's basketball team">Villanova</a>, their team bus struck the rear of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport-utility_vehicle" title="Sport-utility vehicle">sport-utility vehicle</a>, causing the SUV to veer off the highway and overturn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allen20170207_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-allen20170207-54">[54]</a></sup> The team and its staff got off the bus to assist the two occupants of the SUV, who were taken to a hospital, then boarded another bus to finish their journey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allen20170207_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-allen20170207-54">[54]</a></sup> No one aboard the bus requested medical attention,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allen20170207_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-allen20170207-54">[54]</a></sup> but when the Hoyas met Villanova at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Pavilion" title="The Pavilion">The Pavilion</a> the following afternoon, Tre Campbell sat out with a banged knee and John Thompson III  was observed hobbling along the sideline in apparent pain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> The Wildcats missed six of their first seven three-point attempts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> but then Villanova senior guard <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josh_Hart_(basketball)" title="Josh Hart (basketball)">Josh Hart</a> sparked an offensive surge by hitting three three-pointers and scoring 17 first-half points;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> Villanova took a 17-point first-half lead<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> and still led 43–28 at halftime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> In the second half, Hart fell silent on offense and the Hoyas made a comeback bid, mounting a 17–4 scoring run that cut a Wildcat 17-point lead to 60–58 with 3:49 left to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> With Georgetown threatening an upset, Hart regained his form on offense, hitting two clutch shots, a three-pointer and a layup, to give the Wildcats a 70–61 lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> Hart finished with a game-high 25 points and Villanova won 75–64<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> for its 48th straight victory at The Pavilion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> Peak scored 21 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> and Pryor had 20 points and nine rebounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170208_55-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170208-55">[55]</a></sup> but the back-to-back losses dropped Georgetown to 13–12 overall and 4–8 in the Big East.
</p><p>After a safer and much less eventful return trip to Washington, the Hoyas beat Marquette at the Verizon Center. Georgetown shot 53.7 percent from the field as a team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and no fewer than three Hoyas scored 20 points or more: Jesse Govan, Rodney Pryor, and L. J. Peak combined for 23-of-42 (54.7 percent) shooting, and Govan had a game-high 23 points along with eight rebounds, Pryor finished with a double-double (20 points and 10 rebounds), and Peak scored 20 points, including the 1,000th point of his collegiate career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170211_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170211-57">[57]</a></sup> Third in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> in three-point shooting at 42.4 percent, the Golden Eagles managed only 3-of-14 (21.4 percent) from beyond the arc against Georgetown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170211_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170211-57">[57]</a></sup> It was Georgetown's last win of the season and the 278th and final win of John Thompson III's 13-year tenure as Georgetown's head coach.
</p><p>After an eight-day break in action, Georgetown went back on the road for its eighth game of the season against a ranked opponent, facing No. 20 Creighton. Led by redshirt junior guard <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Foster_(basketball)" title="Marcus Foster (basketball)">Marcus Foster</a> – who sank four three-pointers and scored a game-high 35 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> – the Bluejays shot 53 percent from the field compared to only 38.5 percent for the Hoyas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> who managed only a 3-for-22 (13.6 percent) performance from three-point range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> Creighton led 41–33 at halftime<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> and went on a 19–6 scoring run in the second half to take a 60–44 lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> The Hoyas appeared to be mounting a comeback, closing to 66–55, when their shooting went cold and they went scoreless for the next ​<span class="frac nowrap">4<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> minutes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> as Creighton cruised to an 87–70 win. L. J. Peak scored a team-high 23 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor finished with 16,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> and Jesse Govan had 12,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> while Akoy Agau had nine points, nine rebounds, and three blocked shots, but also five turnovers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup>  The Hoyas entered the game as one of the Big East's best defensive teams, but the 87 points the Bluejays scored were the second-most Georgetown had given up all season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup> and Creighton posted the third-highest shooting percentage of any team that had faced the Hoyas during the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170219_58-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170219-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>Three more losses followed in a game at the Verizon Center against DePaul and road games against St. John's and Seton Hall. The DePaul game broke a 10-game losing streak for the Blue Demons<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170222_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170222-59">[59]</a></sup> and a six-game Georgetown winning streak against DePaul,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170222_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170222-59">[59]</a></sup> and it was only the second time in the last 22 meetings between the schools that DePaul had beaten Georgetown. Rodney Pryor scored 14 points against DePaul,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170222_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170222-59">[59]</a></sup> had 22 points including five three-pointers against St. John's,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170225_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170225-60">[60]</a></sup> and finished with 11 against Seton Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170228_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170228-61">[61]</a></sup> In the DePaul game, Jesse Govan had 18 points<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170222_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170222-59">[59]</a></sup> and Marcus Derrickson had 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170222_59-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170222-59">[59]</a></sup> L. J. Peak scored 20 points against St. John's<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170225_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170225-60">[60]</a></sup> and 15 against Seton Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170228_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170228-61">[61]</a></sup>  Against St. John's, Jesse Govan scored 13<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20170225_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20170225-62">[62]</a></sup> and Kaleb Johnson added 11.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxscore20170225_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxscore20170225-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Hoyas closed out the regular season by hosting No. 2 Villanova at the Verizon Center. Villanova led 38–28 at halftime,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> but Georgetown cut the Wildcats′ lead to four points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> 39–35,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbyplay20170304_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-playbyplay20170304-64">[64]</a></sup> with 16:42 remaining in the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbyplay20170304_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-playbyplay20170304-64">[64]</a></sup> Villanova was shooting only 34.8 percent from the field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> on pace for a season low,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> and holding a 46–39 lead with 11:50 remaining in the game<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> when the Wildcat shooters began to find the range.
