With a little over seven minutes remaining, Wildcat senior guard Josh Hart hit two consecutive three-pointers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> to give Villanova a decisive 60–45 lead,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playbyplay20170304_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-playbyplay20170304-64">[64]</a></sup> and the game degenerated into a rout from there, as Villanova scored on 15 of 17 possessions<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> and made 12 of its final 16 shots<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> – improving its shooting percentage from the field to 46.3 percent for the game<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> – on the way to an 81–55 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> Rodney Pryor led Georgetown with 21 points;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> he was the only Georgetown player to score in double figures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> and the Hoyas committed 20 turnovers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-12"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> It was Villanova's fifth straight win against Georgetown, the longest winning streak ever in the rivalry between the schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-13"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Georgetown's regular season ended with a five-game losing streak and losses in seven of its final eight games, and the Hoyas posted a regular-season record of 14–17 overall and 5–13 in the Big East, good for a ninth-place conference finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-14"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> It was the team's worst conference record since a 4–12 finish in the original Big East in <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2003–04 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">the 2003–2004 season</a>, and its worst conference finish since it finished in 11th place in the original Big East in <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2008–09 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2008–2009</a>. In reporting the results of the final game against Villanova, the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> referred to "the disaster of Thompson′s 13th season on the Hilltop [i.e., at Georgetown],"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-15"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> and when a reporter tried to ask John Thompson III questions about the future of the Georgetown men's basketball program as it faced a likely second consecutive losing season, a team spokesman interrupted, saying "Leave it to game-related questions, please."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-16"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_East_Tournament">Big East Tournament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Big East Tournament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2017_Big_East_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2017 Big East Men's Basketball Tournament">2017 Big East Men's Basketball Tournament</a></div>
<p>With a No. 9 seed in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Big_East_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2017 Big East Men's Basketball Tournament">2017 Big East Tournament</a> at Madison Square Garden, Georgetown faced eighth-seeded St. John's in the first round. Both schools were charter members of the original Big East Conference when it was created in <a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1979–80 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1979</a>, and it was their seventh meeting in the tournament since it began in <a href="/wiki/1980_Big_East_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="1980 Big East Men's Basketball Tournament">1980</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> Former Georgetown head coach <a href="/wiki/John_Thompson_(basketball)" title="John Thompson (basketball)">John Thompson, Jr.</a>, and former Georgetown great <a href="/wiki/Allen_Iverson" title="Allen Iverson">Allen Iverson</a>, both members of the <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame</a>, attended the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> In the original Big East's heyday in the mid-1980s, when St. John's head coach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chris_Mullin_(basketball)" title="Chris Mullin (basketball)">Chris Mullin</a> had played for the Red Storm and John Thompson III's father, John Thompson Jr., had coached the Hoyas, the two schools had been national powers and great rivals, and both teams entered the game aware of this history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> St. John's made only five of its first 21 shots from the field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-3"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> but led 38–34 at halftime,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-4"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> and also led for most of the second half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-5"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> With 8:35 left to play and St. John's ahead 59–55, the game briefly took on the character of the very physical games of the original Big East in the 1980s when Red Storm junior forward Amar Alibegović fouled L. J. Peak hard under the basket and a shoving match ensued between several players, resulting in the officials calling a <a href="/wiki/Flagrant_foul" title="Flagrant foul">flagrant foul</a> against Alibegović and <a href="/wiki/Technical_foul" title="Technical foul">technical fouls</a> against both Chris Mullin and Georgetown assistant coach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing,_Jr." title="Patrick Ewing, Jr.">Patrick Ewing, Jr.</a>, a former Georgetown player whose father, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing" title="Patrick Ewing">Patrick Ewing</a>, had played against Mullin as Georgetown's center at the peak of the 1980s rivalry between the teams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-6"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> After the scuffle, Peak made one free throw to cut the Red Storm's lead to 59–56.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-7"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> After that, the Hoyas got within one point of St. John's three times but could never take the lead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-8"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> The Red Storm led 74–68 with three minutes to play, but did not score again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-9"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> In Georgetown's final possession, which began with 6.6 seconds remaining and St. John's clinging to a 74–73 lead,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-10"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> both Peak and Marcus Derrickson missed close-in shots, allowing St. John's to hang on for a 74–73 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-11"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> Georgetown's season came to an end, while St. John's snapped a six-year losing streak in the Big East Tournament<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-12"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> and moved on to face Villanova in the quarterfinals the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-13"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> The Red Storm finished shooting 37.7 percent from the field overall,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-14"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> including 5-for-20 (25 percent) from three-point range,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-15"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> while the Hoyas shot 45.8 percent from the field overall<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-16"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> and made five of their 21 three-point shots (23.8 percent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-17"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> Playing in their last game for Georgetown, Peak scored a game-high 24 points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-18"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> 22 of them in the second half,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-19"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> and Rodney Pryor contributed 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170308_66-20"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170308-66">[66]</a></sup> Derrickson scored 11 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>With a record of 14–18 and having lost their last six games and eight of their last nine, Georgetown received no invitation to either the <a href="/wiki/2017_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2017 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">NCAA Tournament</a> or the <a href="/wiki/2017_National_Invitation_Tournament" title="2017 National Invitation Tournament">National Invitation Tournament</a> for the second straight year. It was the first time Georgetown had two consecutive losing seasons since <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1971–72 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1971–1972</a> and <a href="/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1972–73 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1972–1973</a>, and the first time the Hoyas had received an invitation to neither the NCAA Tournament or the NIT in two consecutive seasons since <a href="/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1972–73 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1973</a> and <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1973–74 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1974</a>. For the second straight season, the Hoyas never made the Top 25 in either the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associated_Press_Poll" title="Associated Press Poll">Associated Press Poll</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Coaches_Poll" title="Coaches Poll">Coaches Poll</a> – the first time that had happened in consecutive seasons since <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2002–03 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2002-2003</a> and <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2003–04 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2003-2004</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="John_Thompson_III_fired">John Thompson III fired</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: John Thompson III fired">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The failure of the 2016–2017 team, coming on the heels of a similar failure the previous season, left the Georgetown basketball program in turmoil. In his 13 years at Georgetown, John Thompson had an overall record of 278–151, with 11 winning seasons,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamariahoffman20170324_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-santamariahoffman20170324-68">[68]</a></sup> eight appearances in the NCAA Tournament and three in the NIT. Since the notorious loss<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup> to 15th-seeded <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Florida_Gulf_Coast_Eagles_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2012–13 Florida Gulf Coast Eagles men's basketball team">Florida Gulf Coast</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2013 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2013 NCAA Tournament</a>, however, Georgetown had endured the worst four-year stretch of his tenure as head coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamariahoffman20170324_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-santamariahoffman20170324-68">[68]</a></sup> Those four years coincided with the first four seasons of the new Big East Conference; it consisted of a group of schools brought in from <a href="/wiki/Mid-major" title="Mid-major">mid-major</a> conferences combined with some of the less-competitive teams from the original Big East, and the Hoyas and their fans had expected the team to dominate the new conference as its flagship program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> Instead, over those four years the Hoyas had posted an overall record of 69–62,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preston20170324_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-preston20170324-71">[71]</a></sup> and their 32–40 Big East record was third-worst in the conference;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamariahoffman20170324_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-santamariahoffman20170324-68">[68]</a></sup> the Hoyas had no regular-season or conference-tournament championships in the new Big East,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> had missed the NCAA Tournament in three of the new conference's four seasons, had lost in the second game of their lone NCAA appearance – as well as in the second game of their only NIT appearance – and had finished with two consecutive losing seasons in which they had no postseason play whatsoever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamariahoffman20170324_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-santamariahoffman20170324-68">[68]</a></sup> For the second year in a row, the team had an up-and-down early season and collapsed in February; the 2016-2017 season ended with six consecutive losses, including to DePaul and St. John's – both long the cellar-dwellers of the Big East – and the team's 14-18 record was the worst for Georgetown since the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1971–72 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1971-1972 team</a>'s dismal 3–23 finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamariahoffman20170324_68-4"><a href="#cite_note-santamariahoffman20170324-68">[68]</a></sup> Although Thompson emphasized defense, the Hoyas′ defense had been mediocre over its four years in the new Big East, never ranking higher than 110th among the 351 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">NCAA Division I</a> teams in defensive efficiency,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> and the 2016–2017 squad's defense statistics were poor: 116th in the defensive efficiency<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-3"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> and 302nd in fouls committed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-4"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> while allowing opponents 10 offensive rebounds per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-5"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> On offense, the Hoyas had gone five seasons without ever ranking in the top 50 teams in offensive efficiency,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-6"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> and in three seasons had ranked worse than 100th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-7"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>By late February, signs began to appear in the student section at the Verizon Center and on the road at Madison Square Garden reading "Fire Thompson" and "Degioia Do Your Job" – a plea for Georgetown University President <a href="/wiki/John_J._DeGioia" title="John J. DeGioia">John J. DeGioia</a> to fire Thompson – and cheers of "Fire Thompson!" became common from the stands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-8"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehoya20170317_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-thehoya20170317-73">[73]</a></sup> In early March, Georgetown students launched a petition demanding that the university fire Thompson;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamariahoffman20170324_68-5"><a href="#cite_note-santamariahoffman20170324-68">[68]</a></sup> it garnered 1,700 signatures by mid-March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehoya20170317_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-thehoya20170317-73">[73]</a></sup> Adding fuel to the fire, Thompson's attempt to address Georgetown's lack of a true <a href="/wiki/Point_guard" title="Point guard">point guard</a> since the graduation of <a href="/wiki/Markel_Starks" title="Markel Starks">Markel Starks</a> in 2014 by recruiting <a href="/wiki/Tremont_Waters" title="Tremont Waters">Tremont Waters</a>, an elite point guard prospect, for the following season failed when Waters requested his release from Georgetown on March 11,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> highlighting to the fan base how much of its star power the Georgetown program had lost since its 2007 Final Four appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehoya20170317_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-thehoya20170317-73">[73]</a></sup> More negative publicity arose when school financial disclosures revealed that Thompson had received annual pay increases from 2008 to through 2014, resulting in a salary of $3.6 million a year that likely made him one of the ten most highly compensated college basketball coaches in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Amid a rising chorus of criticism by Georgetown students and alumni of Thompson's performance, and press articles by students and <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> describing dissatisfaction among Georgetown students and alumni with the direction of the men's basketball program,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamariahoffman20170324_68-6"><a href="#cite_note-santamariahoffman20170324-68">[68]</a></sup> Georgetown University announced on March 23 that it had fired Thompson, bringing his 13-year tenure as head coach to an end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tracy20170323_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-tracy20170323-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>When Thompson arrived at Georgetown to take charge of the program in <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2004–05 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2004</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tracy20170323_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-tracy20170323-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup> he inherited a team that had finished with a losing record <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2003–04 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">the previous season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup> Also inheriting his predecessor <a href="/wiki/Craig_Esherick" title="Craig Esherick">Craig Esherick</a>′s last recruiting class, which included point guard <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Wallace" title="Jonathan Wallace">Jonathan Wallace</a> and two future NBA players, forward <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Green_(basketball)" title="Jeff Green (basketball)">Jeff Green</a> and center <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hibbert" title="Roy Hibbert">Roy Hibbert</a>, and himself recruiting <a href="/wiki/DaJuan_Summers" title="DaJuan Summers">DaJuan Summers</a>, he had led the Hoyas back to the NCAA Tournament, reaching the Sweet Sixteen in <a href="/wiki/2006_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2006 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2006</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup> and the Final Four in <a href="/wiki/2007_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2007 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2007</a> in his third season with the Hoyas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tracy20170323_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-tracy20170323-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-4"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup> Over the next eight seasons, Georgetown made six NCAA Tournament appearances, but won only three NCAA tournament games, never advancing beyond the Round of 32<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tracy20170323_76-3"><a href="#cite_note-tracy20170323-76">[76]</a></sup> and losing in each case to lower-seeded teams, all but one of them double-digit seeds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20170322_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20170322-77">[77]</a></sup> The loss in <a href="/wiki/2008_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2008 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2008</a>, to 10th-seeded <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Davidson_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2007–08 Davidson Wildcats men's basketball team">Davidson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20170322_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20170322-77">[77]</a></sup> was shocking at the time but in retrospect was understandable, given that Davidson was led by future NBA great <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Curry" title="Stephen Curry">Stephen Curry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preston20170324_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-preston20170324-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-5"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-niessen20170323_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-niessen20170323-78">[78]</a></sup> However, it was the harbinger of what turned out to be a gradual, decade-long slide into mediocrity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-niessen20170323_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-niessen20170323-78">[78]</a></sup> The later losses – to 14th-seeded <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Ohio_Bobcats_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2009–10 Ohio Bobcats men's basketball team">Ohio</a> in <a href="/wiki/2010_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2010 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2010</a>, to 11th-seeded <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_VCU_Rams_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2010–11 VCU Rams men's basketball team">VCU</a> in <a href="/wiki/2011_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2011 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2011</a>, to 11th-seeded <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NC_State_Wolfpack_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2011–12 NC State Wolfpack men's basketball team">North Carolina State</a> in <a href="/wiki/2012_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2012 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2012</a>, and above all<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-niessen20170323_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-niessen20170323-78">[78]</a></sup> to 15th-seeded Florida Gulf Coast in 2013, as well as to fifth-seeded <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Utah_Utes_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2014–15 Utah Utes men's basketball team">Utah</a> in <a href="/wiki/2015_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2015 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2015</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-6"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20170322_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20170322-77">[77]</a></sup> – had no such straightforward explanation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steinberg20170309_69-7"><a href="#cite_note-steinberg20170309-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>While the team that centered around the 2011 recruiting class's Greg Whittington and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otto_Porter_Jr." title="Otto Porter Jr.">Otto Porter Jr.</a> showed signs of potential greatness,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20161212_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20161212-79">[79]</a></sup> it never reached the heights of the 2006–2007 Final Four team, and after Porter departed for the NBA in 2013 after his sophomore season, Thompson's recruiting efforts paid fewer and fewer dividends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20161212_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20161212-79">[79]</a></sup> Thompson remained committed to his "<a href="/wiki/Princeton_offense" title="Princeton offense">Princeton offense</a>" despite its growing obsolescence in the face of the evolution of the college game,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-niessen20170323_78-3"><a href="#cite_note-niessen20170323-78">[78]</a></sup> and his adherence to it harmed his recruiting efforts, as potential recruits sought opportunities elsewhere under systems that better fit their playing style and showcased the athletic abilities that NBA scouts favored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170403_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170403-80">[80]</a></sup> Washington, D.C., and its suburbs remained a hotbed of high-school basketball talent, but Thompson had markedly less success in recruiting Washington-area players than his predecessors John Thompson Jr. and Craig Esherick; observers noted that Villanova had built the dominant team and perennial winner in the new Big East Conference – a team that made deep runs annually in the NCAA Tournament and won the national championship in <a href="/wiki/2010_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2010 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2016</a> – at least partially by recruiting two star players from Washington's Maryland suburbs, guards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josh_Hart_(basketball)" title="Josh Hart (basketball)">Josh Hart</a> from <a href="/wiki/Silver_Spring,_Maryland" title="Silver Spring, Maryland">Silver Spring</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-17"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kris_Jenkins_(basketball)" title="Kris Jenkins (basketball)">Kris Jenkins</a> from <a href="/wiki/Upper_Marlboro,_Maryland" title="Upper Marlboro, Maryland">Upper Marlboro</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ap20170304_63-18"><a href="#cite_note-ap20170304-63">[63]</a></sup> both had grown up as Hoya fans, but Thompson lost out to Villanova head coach <a href="/wiki/Jay_Wright_(basketball)" title="Jay Wright (basketball)">Jay Wright</a> in recruiting Hart and never pursued Jenkins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-9"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> Under Thompson, the program had a high number of players transfer to other schools,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup> finding that under Thompson they had too little playing time and few opportunities to showcase their athleticism.
</p><p>The dismissal of both Greg Whittington and <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Smith_(basketball)" title="Joshua Smith (basketball)">Joshua Smith</a> from the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2013–14 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">2013–14 team</a> could explain that team's failure, but Thompson's declining success in recruiting players who fit into his system and who would develop successfully at the college level began to affect the program's success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-10"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> The highly touted 2014 recruiting class – which included Tre Campbell, Trey Mourning, L. J. Peak, and Paul White – despite some success in <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2014–15 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">its first season</a>, also was notable for is lack of development on the court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20161212_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20161212-79">[79]</a></sup> Only Peak showed progress as a junior,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20161212_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20161212-79">[79]</a></sup> and only Mourning remained at Georgetown for a full four years of collegiate eligibility. The glory years of Georgetown's men's basketball program had become too distant to resonate with potential recruits,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balthazard20170224_70-11"><a href="#cite_note-balthazard20170224-70">[70]</a></sup> and without NBA-caliber talent after Porter's departure,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualhoya20161212_79-4"><a href="#cite_note-casualhoya20161212-79">[79]</a></sup> the once-proud Georgetown program had gone from a perennial national power to consistently mediocre performances that culminated in two straight losing seasons and declining fan interest and attendance at home games;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-preston20170324_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-preston20170324-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-niessen20170323_78-4"><a href="#cite_note-niessen20170323-78">[78]</a></sup> for two straight years, Georgetown had struggled to fill even half the seats for its home games at the Verizon Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehoya20170317_73-3"><a href="#cite_note-thehoya20170317-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Patrick_Ewing_hired">Patrick Ewing hired</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Patrick Ewing hired">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rather than fire Thompson soon after the Hoyas′ season ended, Georgetown waited until two weeks later to announce his termination, by which time some top options for the head coaching position already had accepted offers elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup>  Georgetown athletic director Lee Reed and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tagliabue" title="Paul Tagliabue">Paul Tagliabue</a>, a former Georgetown player and one-time commissioner of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, led the effort to find a new head coach,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup> but observers came to the conclusion that the university had no plan in place for who it wanted to succeed Thompson before it fired him, making the school's search for a successor appear bumbling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-4"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_men%27s_basketball" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish men's basketball">Notre Dame's</a> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Brey" title="Mike Brey">Mike Brey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Musketeers_men%27s_basketball" title="Xavier Musketeers men's basketball">Xavier's</a> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Mack_(basketball)" title="Chris Mack (basketball)">Chris Mack</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Texas_Longhorns_men%27s_basketball" title="Texas Longhorns men's basketball">Texas's</a> <a href="/wiki/Shaka_Smart" title="Shaka Smart">Shaka Smart</a> all rebuffed Georgetown's inquiries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-5"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Crimson_men%27s_basketball" title="Harvard Crimson men's basketball">Harvard</a>′s <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Amaker" title="Tommy Amaker">Tommy Amaker</a> privately expressed disinterest in the job because of his concerns over internal politics at Georgetown, fearing that the influence that John Thompson III's father, John Thompson Jr., still wielded over the program despite having resigned as head coach in <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1998–99 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">January 1999</a> could lead to a negative political environment for any new head coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-6"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup> Georgetown informed recently fired <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Hoosiers_men%27s_basketball" title="Indiana Hoosiers men's basketball">Indiana</a> head coach <a href="/wiki/Tom_Crean_(basketball)" title="Tom Crean (basketball)">Tom Crean</a> that he was not a candidate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-7"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup> but the names of <a href="/wiki/Providence_Friars_men%27s_basketball" title="Providence Friars men's basketball">Providence's</a> <a href="/wiki/Ed_Cooley" title="Ed Cooley">Ed Cooley</a> – who made clear that he had no desire to leave Providence<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-8"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup> – <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island_Rams_men%27s_basketball" title="Rhode Island Rams men's basketball">Rhode Island's</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danny_Hurley" title="Danny Hurley">Danny Hurley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers_men%27s_basketball" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers men's basketball">Minnesota's</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Pitino" title="Richard Pitino">Richard Pitino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_Blue_Devils_men%27s_basketball" title="Duke Blue Devils men's basketball">Duke</a> assistant coach <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeff_Capel" title="Jeff Capel">Jeff Capel</a>, <a href="/wiki/USC_Trojans_men%27s_basketball" title="USC Trojans men's basketball">USC's</a> <a href="/wiki/Andy_Enfield" title="Andy Enfield">Andy Enfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Gamecocks_men%27s_basketball" title="South Carolina Gamecocks men's basketball">South Carolina's</a> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Martin_(basketball)" title="Frank Martin (basketball)">Frank Martin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets" title="Charlotte Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</a> assistant coach and Georgetown alumnus <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing" title="Patrick Ewing">Patrick Ewing</a> all were mentioned in the swirl of media speculation that followed Thompson's firing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170402_81-9"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170402-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 3, 2017, Georgetown announced that it had hired Patrick Ewing as its next head basketball coach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Generally regarded as the greatest player in Georgetown history, Ewing had been Georgetown's star center from <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1981–82 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1981</a> to <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team" title="1984–85 Georgetown Hoyas men's basketball team">1985</a>, leading the Hoyas to three appearances in the NCAA Tournament championship game and the <a href="/wiki/1984_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="1984 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">1984</a> national championship, then going on to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naismith_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Basketball Hall of Fame">Naismith Basketball Hall of Fame</a> NBA career as a player from 1985 to 2002 and as an assistant coach from 2002 to 2017. It was Ewing's first head coaching job at any level of basketball, and it marked his first foray into college basketball since his graduation from Georgetown in 1985.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wrap-up">Wrap-up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Wrap-up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rodney Pryor completed his only season as a Hoya as the team's leading scorer for the year; he started all 32 games, shooting 48.0 percent from the field overall and 41.2 percent in three-pointers, averaging a team-high 18.0 points and leading the team with 5.0 rebounds per game. L. J. Peak also started all 32 games, and he averaged 16.3 points and 3.8 rebounds per game, shooting 48.1 percent from the field overall and 32.7 percent from three-point range. Jesse Govan played in every game, starting 21 of them, shooting 53.0 percent in field-goal attempts and 40.0 percent from three-point range, and he averaged 10.1 points and 5.0 rebounds per game. Marcus Derrickson played in 28 games and started 17 of them, averaging 8.3 points per game on 43.2 percent field-goal shooting overall and 34.4 percent from three-point range, and he had 4.4 rebounds per game. In his only season in action with the Hoyas, Akoy Agau appeared in all 32 games and started eight of them; he ended the season with a field-goal percentage of 50.6 and with per-game averages of 4.5 points and 4.3 rebounds. Bradley Hayes appeared in 25 games, starting 11 of them, and he finished with 4.2 points and 4.0 rebounds per game, shooting 53.4 percent from the field. Jagan Moseley started 20 of the 31 games he played in, and he averaged 4.2 points per game on 45.0 percent shooting from the field – 24.3 percent from beyond the arc – and grabbed 2.2 rebounds per game. Playing in all 32 games, Jonathan Mulmore had 12 starts and averaged 3.6 points and 1.4 rebounds per game, shooting 35.7 percent overall and 34.5 percent in three-pointers. Tre Campbell averaged 3.5 points and 1.2 rebounds in the 20 games he played in, all off the bench, and shot 38.7 percent from the field overall and 34.3 percent from three-point range, while Kaleb Johnson started twice in his 30 appearances, shooting 44.2 percent from the field overall and 25.0 percent in three-pointers, averaging 2.3 points per game and pulling down an average of 1.3 rebounds per game. Reggie Cameron played in 17 games, all off the bench, averaging 1.7 points and 0.9 rebound, and Trey Mourning played in only 10 games, all as a reserve, averaging 0.8 point per game. Before his mid-season transfer, Isaac Copeland played in seven games, started five, and averaged 5.5 points and 3.3 rebounds per game, shooting 27.5 percent from the field. Walk-ons Ra'Mond Hines and George Muresan each played in five games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rodney Pryor, Bradley Hayes, and Reggie Cameron all graduated in 2017. In addition to his lone year at Georgetown, Pryor played for <a href="/wiki/Robert_Morris_Colonials_men%27s_basketball" title="Robert Morris Colonials men's basketball">Robert Morris</a> in <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Robert_Morris_Colonials_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2014–15 Robert Morris Colonials men's basketball team">2014–2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Robert_Morris_Colonials_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2015–16 Robert Morris Colonials men's basketball team">2015–2016</a>, and in his three-season college career he appeared in 96 games, starting 84, shooting 46.5 percent overall from the field and 38.1 percent from three-point range and averaging 17.1 points and 5.8 rebounds per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Hayes played parts of five seasons for Georgetown; an afterthought for the first three, he had his breakout game against <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Eastern_Washington_Eagles_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2014–15 Eastern Washington Eagles men's basketball team">Eastern Washington</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015_NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Basketball_Tournament" title="2015 NCAA Division I Men's Basketball Tournament">2015 NCAA Tournament</a>, and he made his greatest contributions to the team over the next two seasons. He finished his career having played in 94 games, starting 38 of them, shooting 53.4 percent from the field and averaging 4.0 points and 3.4 rebounds per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Cameron appeared in 104 games in his four years at Georgetown, starting 18 of them, and finished his college career with a 37.4 shooting percentage from the field overall and 32.6 percent from three-point range, averaging 3.4 points and 1.3 rebounds per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of other players also left the team after the season. L. J. Peak announced on March 21 – two days before the university fired Thompson – that he had decided to forego his senior year of college and enter the <a href="/wiki/2017_NBA_draft" title="2017 NBA draft">2017 NBA draft</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Peak completed his three-season college career with 98 games played, including 76 starts, averaging 12.1 points and 3.1 rebounds per game and shooting 46.1 percent from the field, 33.5 percent from three-point range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> He went undrafted, but played professionally outside the NBA. Isaac Copeland, who had transferred to Nebraska in mid-season, received word that the NCAA had granted him a medical hardship waiver that would permit him to begin play for the Cornhuskers at the beginning of <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Nebraska_Cornhuskers_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2017–18 Nebraska Cornhuskers men's basketball team">the 2017–2018 season</a> after sitting out only one semester.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> In his ​<span class="frac nowrap">2<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> seasons as a Hoya, Copeland had appeared in 73 games and started 49, shooting 50.0 percent from the field and 29.1 percent from beyond the arc, averaging 8.6 points and 4.5 rebounds per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Akoy Agau, after finishing his only season of action with the Hoyas, announced on May 27 that he would transfer to <a href="/wiki/SMU_Mustangs_men%27s_basketball" title="SMU Mustangs men's basketball">SMU</a>, where, as a graduate transfer, he would be eligible to begin play immediately in <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_SMU_Mustangs_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2017–18 SMU Mustangs men's basketball team">the 2017–2018 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> In early August 2017, Georgetown announced that Tre Campbell, amid rumors that he would miss the 2017–2018 season due to injuries he sustained in the February 2017 bus accident and other injuries he suffered during the 2017 offseason, would remain on scholarship but had been released from the basketball program for personal reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> He completed his three seasons on the team having played in 84 games, starting 21 of them, averaging 3.7 points per game on 34.7 percent shooting from the field overall and 31.7 percent in three-pointers, and he grabbed 1.4 rebounds per game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Campbell remained at school at Georgetown, sitting out the 2017-2018 basketball season and graduating in 2018, and with a year of college eligibility remaining after his graduation, announced on May 8, 2018, that he would transfer to <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina_Gamecocks_men%27s_basketball" title="South Carolina Gamecocks men's basketball">South Carolina</a> where, as a graduate transfer, he would be eligible to begin play immediately in <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_South_Carolina_Gamecocks_men%27s_basketball_team" title="2018–19 South Carolina Gamecocks men's basketball team">the 2018-2019 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Rumors arose in mid-March that junior Trey Mourning, after limited playing time in three seasons as a Hoya and spending the last two games of the season on the sideline wearing a suit, would transfer from Georgetown,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> although in June the news broke that Mourning would return to Georgetown for his senior year after all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the end of the season, and with a new coach, the Hoyas faced an uncertain future. The failure of most of John Thompson III's recent recruiting efforts and the loss of the team's top scorers left Georgetown with what <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> writer Pete Thamel described as a "program [that] is already buzz-less, lacking an on-court identity," and with "a roster so devoid of talent it would make 1980s Hoyas weep."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170403_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170403-80">[80]</a></sup> Ewing was untested as a head coach and lacked familiarity with modern college basketball,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170403_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170403-80">[80]</a></sup> and his hiring was viewed as a great gamble that had a high potential payoff if he quickly learned how to navigate the complexities of college recruiting and player development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170403_80-3"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170403-80">[80]</a></sup> As one of his first steps, Ewing attempted to re-recruit Tremont Waters, but Waters ultimately spurned his efforts, and in June he committed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LSU_Tigers_men%27s_basketball" title="LSU Tigers men's basketball">LSU</a> instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Georgetown's program was in decline, and Waters's decision demonstrated how little attraction it held for nationally prominent recruits, The Hoyas were relying on Ewing to lay a foundation for it to return to national greatness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thamel20170403_80-4"><a href="#cite_note-thamel20170403-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Roster">Roster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016%E2%80%9317_Georgetown_Hoyas_men%27s_basketball_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Roster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:left;"><span data-sort-value="Peak, L. J."><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/L._J._Peak" title="L. J. Peak">L. J. Peak</a></span></span></span>
